<h1>
<a id="user-content-aaa--tacacs-configuration-and-show" class="anchor" href="#aaa--tacacs-configuration-and-show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>AAA
& TACACS+ Configuration And Show
</h1>
<p>
This section captures the various show commands & configuration commands
that are applicable for the AAA (Authentication, Authorization, and
Accounting) module. Admins can configure the type of authentication
(local or remote tacacs based) required for the users and also the
authentication failthrough and fallback options. Following show command
displays the current running configuration related to the AAA.
</p>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-aaa-configuration-and-show" class="anchor" href="#aaa-configuration-and-show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>AAA
Configuration And Show
</h2>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-aaa-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#aaa-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>AAA
show commands
</h3>
<p>
This command is used to view the Authentication, Authorization &
Accounting settings that are configured in the network node.
</p>
<p>
<strong>show aaa</strong><br> This command displays the AAA settings
currently present in the network node
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show aaa
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show aaa
AAA authentication login local (default)
AAA authentication failthrough True (default)
AAA authentication fallback True (default)
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-aaa-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#aaa-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>AAA
config commands
</h3>
<p>
This sub-section explains all the possible CLI based configuration
options for the AAA module. The list of commands/sub-commands possible
for aaa is given below.
</p>
<pre><code>Command: aaa authentication
         sub-commands:
           aaa authentication failthrough
           aaa authentication fallback
           aaa authentication login
</code></pre>
<p>
<strong>aaa authentication failthrough</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to either enable or disable the failthrough option.
This command is useful when user has configured more than one tacacs+
server and when user has enabled tacacs+ authentication. When
authentication request to the first server fails, this configuration
allows to continue the request to the next server. When this
configuration is enabled, authentication process continues through all
servers configured. When this is disabled and if the authentication
request fails on first server, authentication process will stop and the
login will be disallowed.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config aaa authentication failthrough
enable\|disable\|default
</p>
<pre><code>     Allow AAA fail-through [enable | disable | default]
     enable - this allows the AAA module to process with local authentication if remote authentication fails.
     disbale - this disallows the AAA module to proceed further if remote authentication fails.
     default - this re-configures the default value, which is "enable".
</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo -i
root@sonic:~# config aaa authentication failthrough enable
root@sonic:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>aaa authentication fallback</strong>
</p>
<p>
The command is not used at the moment. When the tacacs+ authentication
fails, it falls back to local authentication by default.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config aaa authentication fallback enable\|disable\|default
</p>
<pre><code> Allow AAA fallback [enable | disable | default]
</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@sonic:~# config aaa authentication fallback enable
root@sonic:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>aaa authentication login</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to either configure whether AAA should use local
database or remote tacacs+ database for user authentication. By default,
AAA uses local database for authentication. New users can be
added/deleted using the linux commands (note that the configuration done
using linux commands are not preserved during reboot). Admin can enable
remote tacacs+ server based authentication by selecting the
AUTH\_PROTOCOL as tacacs+ in this command. Admins need to configure the
tacacs+ server accordingly and ensure that the connectivity to tacacas+
server is available via the management interface. Once if the admins
choose the remote authentication based on tacacs+ server, all user
logins will be authenticated by the tacacs+ server. If the
authentication fails, AAA will check the "failthrough" configuration and
authenticates the user based on local database if failthrough is
enabled.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> Switch login authentication \[ {tacacs+, local} \| default \]
</p>
<pre><code>Switch login authentication [ {tacacs+, local} | default ]
tacacs+ - This enables remote authentication based on tacacs+
local - this disables remote authentication and uses local authentication
default - reset back to default value, which is nothing but the "local" authentication
</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@sonic:~# config aaa authentication login tacacs+
root@sonic:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-tacacs-configuration-and-show" class="anchor" href="#tacacs-configuration-and-show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>TACACS+
Configuration And Show
</h2>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-tacacs-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#tacacs-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>TACACS+
show commands
</h3>
<p>
<strong>show tacacs</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the global configuration fields and the list of
all tacacs servers and their correponding configurations.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show tacacs
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  TACPLUS global auth_type pap (default)
  TACPLUS global timeout 99
  TACPLUS global passkey &lt;EMPTY_STRING&gt; (default)

  TACPLUS_SERVER address 10.11.12.14
               priority 9
               tcp_port 50
               auth_type mschap
               timeout 10
               passkey testing789

  TACPLUS_SERVER address 10.0.0.9
               priority 1
               tcp_port 49
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-tacacs-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#tacacs-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>TACACS+
Config commands
</h3>
<p>
This sub-section explains the command "config tacacs" and its
sub-commands that are used to configure the following tacacs+
parameters. Some of the parameters like authtype, passkey and timeout
can be either configured at per server level or at global level (global
value will be applied if there no server level configuration)
</p>
<ol>
<li>
Add/Delete the tacacs+ server details.
</li>
<li>
authtype - global configuration that is applied to all servers if there
is no server specific configuration.
</li>
<li>
default - reset the authtype or passkey or timeout to the default
values.
</li>
<li>
passkey - global configuration that is applied to all servers if there
is no server specific configuration.
</li>
<li>
timeout - global configuration that is applied to all servers if there
is no server specific configuration.
</li>
</ol>
<p>
<strong>config tacacs add</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to add a TACACS+ server to the tacacs server list.
Note that more than one tacacs+ (maximum of seven) can be added in the
device. When user tries to login, tacacs client shall contact the
servers one by one. When any server times out, device will try the next
server one by one based on the priority value configured for that
server. When this command is executed, the configured tacacs+ server
addresses are updated in /etc/pam.d/common-auth-sonic configuration file
which is being used by tacacs service.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config tacacs add \<ip\_address\> \[-t\|--timeout SECOND\]
\[-k\|--key SECRET\] \[-a\|--type TYPE\] \[-o\|--port PORT\] \[-p\|--pri
PRIORITY\] \[-m\|--use-mgmt-vrf\]
</p>
<p>
<strong>Arguments:</strong>
</p>
<p>
ip\_address - TACACS+ server IP address. timeout - Transmission timeout
interval in seconds, range 1 to 60, default 5 key - Shared secret type -
Authentication type, "chap" or "pap" or "mschap" or "login", default is
"pap". port - TCP port range is 1 to 65535, default 49 pri - Priority,
priority range 1 to 64, default 1. use-mgmt-vrf - this means that the
server is part of Management vrf, default is "no vrf"
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config tacacs add 10.11.12.13 -t 10 -k testing789 -a mschap -o 50 -p 9
root@T1-2:~#

  Example Server Configuration in /etc/pam.d/common-auth-sonic configuration file:

  auth    [success=done new_authtok_reqd=done default=ignore]     pam_tacplus.so server=10.11.12.14:50 secret=testing789 login=mschap timeout=10  try_first_pass
  auth    [success=done new_authtok_reqd=done default=ignore]     pam_tacplus.so server=10.11.12.24:50 secret=testing789 login=mschap timeout=987654321098765433211
  0987  try_first_pass
  auth    [success=done new_authtok_reqd=done default=ignore]     pam_tacplus.so server=10.0.0.9:49 secret= login=mschap timeout=5  try_first_pass
  auth    [success=done new_authtok_reqd=done default=ignore]     pam_tacplus.so server=10.0.0.8:49 secret= login=mschap timeout=5  try_first_pass
  auth    [success=done new_authtok_reqd=done default=ignore]     pam_tacplus.so server=10.11.12.13:50 secret=testing789 login=mschap timeout=10  try_first_pass
  auth    [success=1 default=ignore]      pam_unix.so nullok try_first_pass

     NOTE: In the above example, the servers are stored (sorted) based on the priority value configured for the server.

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config tacacs delete</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to delete the tacacs+ servers configured.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config tacacs delete \<ip\_address\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config tacacs delete 10.11.12.13
root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config tacacs authtype</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to modify the global value for the TACACS+
authtype. When user has not configured server specific authtype, this
global value shall be used for that server.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config tacacs authtype chap\|pap\|\|mschap\|login
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config tacacs authtype mschap
root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config tacacs default</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to reset the global value for authtype or passkey
or timeout to default value. Default for authtype is "pap", default for
passkey is EMPTY\_STRING and default for timeout is 5 seconds.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config tacacs default authtype\|passkey\|timeout
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config tacacs default authtype
This will reset the global authtype back to the default value "pap".
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config tacacs passkey</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to modify the global value for the TACACS+ passkey.
When user has not configured server specific passkey, this global value
shall be used for that server.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config tacacs passkey \<pass\_key\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config tacacs passkey testing123
root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config tacacs timeout</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to modify the global value for the TACACS+ timeout.
When user has not configured server specific timeout, this global value
shall be used for that server.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config tacacs timeout \<timeout\_value\_in\_seconds\> valid
values for timeout is 1 to 60 seconds.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config tacacs timeout 60
root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or <a href="#AAA-Configuration-And-Show">Beginning of
this section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-acl-configuration-and-show" class="anchor" href="#acl-configuration-and-show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ACL
Configuration And Show
</h1>
<p>
This section explains the various show commands and configuration
commands available for users.
</p>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-acl-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#acl-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ACL
show commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show acl table</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays either all the ACL tables that are configured or
only the specified "TABLE\_NAME". Output from the command displays the
table name, type of the table, the list of interface(s) to which the
table is bound and the description about the table.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show acl table \[TABLE\_NAME\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show acl table
  Name      Type       Binding          Description
  --------  ---------  ---------------  -------------
  EVERFLOW  MIRROR     Ethernet16       EVERFLOW
                     Ethernet96
                     Ethernet108
                     Ethernet112
                     PortChannel0001
                     PortChannel0002
  SNMP_ACL  CTRLPLANE  SNMP             SNMP_ACL
  DT_ACL_T1 L3         Ethernet0        DATA_ACL_TABLE_1
                     Ethernet4
                     Ethernet112
                     Ethernet116
  SSH_ONLY  CTRLPLANE  SSH              SSH_ONLY

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show acl rule</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the ACL rules present in all the ACL tables or
only the rules present in specified table "TABLE\_NAME" or only the rule
matching the RULE\_ID option. Output from the command gives the
following information about the rules
</p>
<ol>
<li>
Table name - ACL table name to which the rule belongs to.
</li>
<li>
Rule name - ACL rule name
</li>
<li>
Priority - Priority for this rule.
</li>
<li>
Action - Action to be performed if the packet matches with this ACL
rule. It could be either Drop or Permit. Users can choose to have a
default permit rule or default deny rule. In case of default "deny all"
rule, add the permitted rules on top of the deny rule. In case of the
default "permit all" rule, users can add the deny rules on top of it. If
users have not confgured any rule, SONiC allows all traffic (which is
"permit all").
</li>
<li>
Match - The fields from the packet header that need to be matched
against the same present in the incoming traffic.
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show acl rule \[TABLE\_NAME\] \[RULE\_ID\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show acl rule
  Table     Rule          Priority    Action    Match
  --------  ------------  ----------  --------  ------------------
  SNMP_ACL  RULE_1        9999        ACCEPT    IP_PROTOCOL: 17
                                              SRC_IP: 1.1.1.1/32
  SSH_ONLY  RULE_1        9999        ACCEPT    IP_PROTOCOL: 6
                                              SRC_IP: 1.1.1.1/32
  SNMP_ACL  DEFAULT_RULE  1           DROP      ETHER_TYPE: 2048
  SSH_ONLY  DEFAULT_RULE  1           DROP      ETHER_TYPE: 2048

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-acl-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#acl-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ACL
config commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains the list of configuration options available
for ACL module. Note that there is no direct command to add or delete or
modify the ACL table and ACL rule. Existing ACL tables and ACL rules can
be updated by specifying the ACL rules in json file formats and
configure those files using this CLI command.
</p>
<pre><code>Command :acl
          update
             full
             incremental
</code></pre>
<p>
<strong>config acl update full</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is to update the rules in all the tables or in one specific
table in full. If a table\_name is provided, the operation will be
restricted in the specified table. All existing rules in the specified
table or all tables will be removed. New rules loaded from file will be
installed. If the table\_name is specified, only rules within that table
will be removed and new rules in that table will be installed. If the
table\_name is not specified, all rules from all tables will be removed
and only the rules present in the input file will be added.
</p>
<p>
The command does not modify anything in the list of acl tables. It
modifies only the rules present in those pre-existing tables.
</p>
<p>
In order to create acl tables, either follow the config\_db.json method
or minigraph method to populate the list of ACL tables.
</p>
<p>
After creating tables, either the config\_db.json method or the
minigraph method or the CLI method (explained here) can be used to
populate the rules in those ACL tables.
</p>
<p>
This command updates only the ACL rules and it does not disturb the ACL
tables; i.e.┬áthe output of "show acl table" is not alterted by using
this command; only the output of "show acl rule" will be changed after
this command.
</p>
<p>
When "--session\_name" optional argument is specified, command sets the
session\_name for the ACL table with this mirror session name. It fails
if the specified mirror session name does not exist.
</p>
<p>
When the optional argument "max\_priority" is specified, each rule's
priority is calculated by subtracting its "sequence\_id" value from the
"max\_priority". If this value is not passed, the default
"max\_priority" 10000 is used.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config acl update full FILE\_NAME<br> Some of the possible
options are
</p>
<ol>
<li>
--table\_name \<table\_name\>, Example: config acl update full \"
--table\_name DT\_ACL\_T1 /etc/sonic/acl\_table\_1.json \"
</li>
<li>
--session\_name \<session\_name\>, Example: config acl update full \"
--session\_name mirror\_ses1 /etc/sonic/acl\_table\_1.json \"
</li>
<li>
--max\_priority \<priority\_value\>, Example: config acl update full \"
--max-priority 100 /etc/sonic/acl\_table\_1.json \"
</li>
</ol>
<p>
NOTE: All these optional parameters should be inside the double quotes.
If none of the options are provided, double quotes is not required for
specifying filename alone. Any number of optional parameters can be
configured in the same command.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ config acl update full /etc/sonic/acl_full_snmp_1_2_ssh_4.json
admin@sonic:~$ config acl update full " --table_name SNMP-ACL /etc/sonic/acl_full_snmp_1_2_ssh_4.json "
admin@sonic:~$ config acl update full " --session_name everflow0 /etc/sonic/acl_full_snmp_1_2_ssh_4.json "

This command will remove all rules from all the ACL tables and insert all the rules present in this input file.
Refer the example file [acl_full_snmp_1_2_ssh_4.json](#) that adds two rules for SNMP (Rule1 and Rule2) and one rule for SSH (Rule4)
Refer an example for input file format [here](https://github.com/Azure/sonic-mgmt/blob/master/ansible/roles/test/files/helpers/config_service_acls.sh)
Refer another example [here](https://github.com/Azure/sonic-mgmt/blob/master/ansible/roles/test/tasks/acl/acltb_test_rules_part_1.json)
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config acl update incremental:</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to perform incremental update of ACL rule table.
This command gets existing rules from Config DB and compares with rules
specified in input file and performs corresponding modifications.
</p>
<p>
With respect to DATA ACLs, the command does not assume that new
dataplane ACLs can be inserted in betweeen by shifting existing ACLs in
all ASICs. Therefore, this command performs a full update on dataplane
ACLs. With respect to control plane ACLs, this command performs an
incremental update. If we assume that "file1.json" is the already loaded
ACL rules file and if "file2.json" is the input file that is passed as
parameter for this command, the following requirements are valid for the
input file.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
First copy the file1.json to file2.json.
</li>
<li>
Remove the unwanted ACL rules from file2.json
</li>
<li>
Add the newly required ACL rules into file2.json.
</li>
<li>
Modify the existing ACL rules (that require changes) in file2.json.
</li>
</ol>
<p>
NOTE: If any ACL rule that is already available in file1.json is
required even after this command execution, such rules should remain
unalterted in file2.json. Don't remove them. Note that "incremental" is
working like "full".
</p>
<p>
When "--session\_name" optional argument is specified, command sets the
session\_name for the ACL table with this mirror session name. It fails
if the specified mirror session name does not exist.
</p>
<p>
When the optional argument "max\_priority" is specified, each rule's
priority is calculated by subtracting its "sequence\_id" value from the
"max\_priority". If this value is not passed, the default
"max\_priority" 10000 is used.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config acl update incremental FILE\_NAME Some of the possible
options are
</p>
<ol>
<li>
--session\_name \<session\_name\>, Example: config acl update full \"
--session\_name mirror\_ses1 /etc/sonic/acl\_table\_1.json \"
</li>
<li>
--max-priority \<priority\_value\>, Example: config acl update full \"
--max-priority 100 /etc/sonic/acl\_table\_1.json \"
</li>
</ol>
<p>
NOTE: All these optional parameters should be inside the double quotes.
If none of the options are provided, double quotes is not required for
specifying filename alone. Any number of optional parameters can be
configured in the same command.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ config acl update incremental /etc/sonic/acl_incremental_snmp_1_3_ssh_4.json
admin@sonic:~$ config acl update incremental " --session_name everflow0 /etc/sonic/acl_incremental_snmp_1_3_ssh_4.json "

Refer the example file [acl_incremental_snmp_1_3_ssh_4.json](#) that adds two rules for SNMP (Rule1 and Rule3) and one rule for SSH (Rule4)
When this "incremental" command is executed after "full" command, it has removed SNMP Rule2 and added SNMP Rule3 in the example.
File "acl_full_snmp_1_2_ssh_4.json" has got SNMP Rule1, SNMP Rule2 and SSH Rule4.
File "acl_incremental_snmp_1_3_ssh_4.json" has got SNMP Rule1, SNMP Rule3 and SSH Rule4.
This file is created by copying the file "acl_full_snmp_1_2_ssh_4.json" to "acl_incremental_snmp_1_3_ssh_4.json" and then removing SNMP Rule2 and adding SNMP Rule3.

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or <a href="#ACL-Configuration-And-Show">Beginning of
this section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-arp--ndp" class="anchor" href="#arp--ndp" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ARP
& NDP
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-arp-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#arp-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ARP
show commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show arp</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the ARP entries in the device with following
options.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
Display the entire table.
</li>
<li>
Display the ARP entries learnt on a specific interface.
</li>
<li>
Display the ARP of a specific ip-address.
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show arp \[-if \] \[\] show arp - displays all entries show
arp -if - displays the ARP specific to the specified interface. show arp
- displays the ARP specific to the specicied ip-address.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show arp
 Address          MacAddress            Iface         Vlan
-------------     -----------------     -------       ------
192.168.1.183     88:5a:92:fb:bf:41     Ethernet44    -
192.168.1.175     88:5a:92:fc:95:81     Ethernet28    -
192.168.1.181     e4:c7:22:c1:07:7c     Ethernet40    -
192.168.1.179     88:5a:92:de:a8:bc     Ethernet36    -
192.168.1.118     00:1c:73:3c:de:43     Ethernet64    -
192.168.1.11      00:1c:73:3c:e1:38     Ethernet88    -
192.168.1.161     24:e9:b3:71:3a:01     Ethernet0     -
192.168.1.189     24:e9:b3:9d:57:41     Ethernet56    -
192.168.1.187     74:26:ac:8b:8f:c1     Ethernet52    -
192.168.1.165     88:5a:92:de:a0:7c     Ethernet8     -

Total number of entries 10
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Optionally, you can specify the interface in order to display the ARPs
learnt on that particular interface
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show arp -if Ethernet40
Address          MacAddress          Iface        Vlan
-------------    -----------------   ----------   ------
192.168.1.181    e4:c7:22:c1:07:7c   Ethernet40   -
Total number of entries 1

</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Optionally, you can specify an IP address in order to display only that
particular entry
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show arp 192.168.1.181
Address          MacAddress          Iface        Vlan
-------------    -----------------   ----------   ------
192.168.1.181    e4:c7:22:c1:07:7c   Ethernet40   -
Total number of entries 1
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-ndp-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#ndp-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>NDP
show commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show ndp</strong><br> This command displays either all the IPv6
neighbor mac addresses, or for a particular IPv6 neighbor, or for all
IPv6 neighbors reachable via a specific interface.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ndp \[-if\|--iface \<interface-name.\] \[IP6ADDRESS\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  **ALL IPv6 NEIGHBORS:**
  admin@sonic:~$ show ndp
  Address                   MacAddress         Iface    Vlan    Status
  ------------------------  -----------------  -------  ------  ---------
  fe80::20c:29ff:feb8:b11e  00:0c:29:b8:b1:1e  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  fe80::20c:29ff:feb8:cff0  00:0c:29:b8:cf:f0  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  fe80::20c:29ff:fef9:324   00:0c:29:f9:03:24  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  Total number of entries 3

  **SPECIFIC IPv6 NEIGHBOR**
  admin@sonic:~$ show ndp fe80::20c:29ff:feb8:b11e
  Address                   MacAddress         Iface    Vlan    Status
  ------------------------  -----------------  -------  ------  ---------
  fe80::20c:29ff:feb8:b11e  00:0c:29:b8:b1:1e  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  Total number of entries 1

  **SPECIFIC INTERFACE**
  admin@sonic:~$ show ndp -if eth0
  Address                   MacAddress         Iface    Vlan    Status
  ------------------------  -----------------  -------  ------  ---------
  fe80::20c:29ff:feb8:b11e  00:0c:29:b8:b1:1e  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  fe80::20c:29ff:feb8:cff0  00:0c:29:b8:cf:f0  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  fe80::20c:29ff:fef9:324   00:0c:29:f9:03:24  eth0     -       REACHABLE
  Total number of entries 3

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#Watermark-Configuration-And-Show">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-bgp-configuration-and-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#bgp-configuration-and-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>BGP
Configuration And Show Commands
</h1>
<p>
This section explains all the BGP show commands and BGP configuation
commands that are supported in SONiC.
</p>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-bgp-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#bgp-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>BGP
show commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show ip bgp summary</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the summary of all IPv4 bgp neighbors that are
configured and the corresponding states.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ip bgp summary
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ip bgp summary
BGP router identifier 1.2.3.4, local AS number 65061
RIB entries 6124, using 670 KiB of memory
Peers 2, using 143 KiB of memory

Neighbor        V         AS MsgRcvd MsgSent   TblVer  InQ OutQ Up/Down  State/PfxRcd
192.168.1.161    4 65501   88698  102781        0    0    0 08w5d14h        2
192.168.1.163    4 65502   88698  102780        0    0    0 08w5d14h        2

Total number of neighbors 2
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ip bgp neighbors</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the details of IPv4 & IPv6 BGP neighbors when
no optional argument is specified.
</p>
<p>
When the optional argument IPv4\_address is specified, it displays the
detailed neighbor information about that specific IPv4 neighbor.
</p>
<p>
Command has got additional optional arguments to display only the
advertised routes, or the received routes, or all routes.
</p>
<p>
In order to get details for an IPv6 neigbor, use "show ipv6 bgp neighbor
\<ipv6\_address\>" command.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ip bgp neighbors \[ \[advertised-routes \|
received-routes \| routes\]\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ip bgp neighbors
BGP neighbor is 192.168.1.161, remote AS 65501, local AS 65061, external link
 Description: ARISTA01T0
  BGP version 4, remote router ID 1.2.3.4
  BGP state = Established, up for 08w5d14h
  Last read 00:00:46, hold time is 180, keepalive interval is 60 seconds
  Neighbor capabilities:
    4 Byte AS: advertised and received
    Dynamic: received
    Route refresh: advertised and received(old &amp; new)
    Address family IPv4 Unicast: advertised and received
    Graceful Restart Capabilty: advertised and received
      Remote Restart timer is 120 seconds
      Address families by peer:
        IPv4 Unicast(not preserved)
  Graceful restart informations:
    End-of-RIB send: IPv4 Unicast
    End-of-RIB received: IPv4 Unicast
  Message statistics:
    Inq depth is 0
    Outq depth is 0
                         Sent       Rcvd
    Opens:                  1          1
    Notifications:          0          0
    Updates:            14066          3
    Keepalives:         88718      88698
    Route Refresh:          0          0
    Capability:             0          0
    Total:             102785      88702
  Minimum time between advertisement runs is 30 seconds

 For address family: IPv4 Unicast
  Community attribute sent to this neighbor(both)
  2 accepted prefixes

  Connections established 1; dropped 0
  Last reset never
Local host: 192.168.1.160, Local port: 32961
Foreign host: 192.168.1.161, Foreign port: 179
Nexthop: 192.168.1.160
Nexthop global: fe80::f60f:1bff:fe89:bc00
Nexthop local: ::
BGP connection: non shared network
Read thread: on  Write thread: off
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Optionally, you can specify an IP address in order to display only that
particular neighbor. In this mode, you can optionally specify whether
you want to display all routes advertised to the specified neighbor, all
routes received from the specified neighbor or all routes (received and
accepted) from the specified neighbor.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ip bgp neighbors 192.168.1.161

admin@sonic:~$ show ip bgp neighbors 192.168.1.161 advertised-routes

admin@sonic:~$ show ip bgp neighbors 192.168.1.161 received-routes

admin@sonic:~$ show ip bgp neighbors 192.168.1.161 routes
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ipv6 bgp summary</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the summary of all IPv4 bgp neighbors that are
configured and the corresponding states.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ipv6 bgp summary
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 bgp summary
BGP router identifier 10.1.0.32, local AS number 65100
RIB entries 12809, using 1401 KiB of memory
Peers 8, using 36 KiB of memory

Neighbor        V         AS MsgRcvd MsgSent   TblVer  InQ OutQ Up/Down  State/PfxRcd
fc00::72        4 64600   12588   12591        0    0    0 06:51:17     6402
fc00::76        4 64600   12587    6190        0    0    0 06:51:28     6402
fc00::7a        4 64600   12587    9391        0    0    0 06:51:23     6402
fc00::7e        4 64600   12589   12592        0    0    0 06:51:25     6402

Total number of neighbors 4
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ipv6 bgp neighbors</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the details of one particular IPv6 Border
Gateway Protocol (BGP) neighbor. Option is also available to display
only the advertised routes, or the received routes, or all routes.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ipv6 bgp neighbors (advertised-routes \| received-routes
\| routes)\`
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 bgp neighbors fc00::72 advertised-routes

admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 bgp neighbors fc00::72 received-routes

admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 bgp neighbors fc00::72 routes
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show route-map</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the routing policy that takes precedence over the
other route processes that are configured.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show route-map
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
</li>
</ul>
<pre><code>  admin@T1-2:~$ show route-map
  ZEBRA:
  route-map RM_SET_SRC, permit, sequence 10
    Match clauses:
    Set clauses:
    src 10.12.0.102
    Call clause:
    Action:
    Exit routemap
  ZEBRA:
  route-map RM_SET_SRC6, permit, sequence 10
    Match clauses:
    Set clauses:
    src fc00:1::102
    Call clause:
    Action:
    Exit routemap
  BGP:
  route-map FROM_BGP_SPEAKER_V4, permit, sequence 10
    Match clauses:
    Set clauses:
    Call clause:
    Action:
      Exit routemap
  BGP:
  route-map TO_BGP_SPEAKER_V4, deny, sequence 10
    Match clauses:
    Set clauses:
    Call clause:
    Action:
      Exit routemap
  BGP:
  route-map ISOLATE, permit, sequence 10
    Match clauses:
    Set clauses:
    as-path prepend 65000
    Call clause:
    Action:
    Exit routemap
</code></pre>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-bgp-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#bgp-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>BGP
config commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains the list of configuration options available
for BGP module for both IPv4 and IPv6 BGP neighbors.
</p>
<p>
The list of possible BGP config commands are given below.
</p>
<pre><code>bgp
    shutdown
        all
        neighbor
    startup
        all
        neighbor
</code></pre>
<p>
<strong>config bgp shut down all</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to shutdown all the BGP IPv4 & IPv6 sessions. When
the session is shutdown using this command, BGP state in "show ip bgp
summary" is displayed as "Idle (Admin)"
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> sudo config bgp shutdown all
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Examples:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config bgp shutdown all
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config bgp shutdown </strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is to shut down a BGP session with a neighbor by that
neighbor's IP address or hostname
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> sudo config bgp shutdown ( \| )
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Examples:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config bgp shutdown neighbor 192.168.1.124
</code></pre>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config bgp shutdown neighbor SONIC02SPINE
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config bgp startup all</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to start up all the IPv4 & IPv6 BGP neighbors
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> sudo config bgp startup
all`</p> </li> <li> <p>Examples:</p> <pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config bgp startup all </code></pre> </li> </ul> <p><strong>config bgp startup </strong></p> <p>This command is used to start up the particular IPv4 or IPv6 BGP neighbor using either the IP address or hostname.</p> <ul> <li> <p>Usage:<br> sudo config bgp startup ( | )`
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Examples:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config bgp startup neighbor 192.168.1.124
</code></pre>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config bgp startup neighbor SONIC02SPINE
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#BGP-Configuration-And-Show-Commands">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-ecn-configuration-and-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#ecn-configuration-and-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ECN
Configuration And Show Commands
</h1>
<p>
This section explains all the Explicit Congestion Notification (ECN)
show commands and ECN configuation options that are supported in SONiC.
</p>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-ecn-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#ecn-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ECN
show commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section contains the show commands that are supported in ECN.
</p>
<p>
<strong>show ecn</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the WRED profiles that are configured in the
device.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ecn
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  show ecn
  Profile: **AZURE_LOSSLESS**
  -----------------------  -------
  red_max_threshold        2097152
  red_drop_probability     5
  yellow_max_threshold     2097152
  ecn                      ecn_all
  green_min_threshold      1048576
  red_min_threshold        1048576
  wred_yellow_enable       true
  yellow_min_threshold     1048576
  green_max_threshold      2097152
  green_drop_probability   5
  wred_green_enable        true
  yellow_drop_probability  5
  wred_red_enable          true
  -----------------------  -------

  Profile: **wredprofileabcd**
  -----------------  ---
  red_max_threshold  100
  -----------------  ---

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-ecn-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#ecn-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>ECN
config commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section contains the configuration commands that can configure
the WRED profiles.
</p>
<p>
<strong>config ecn</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command configures the possible fields in a particular WRED profile
that is specified using "-profile" argument. The list of the WRED
profile fields that are configurable is listed in the below "Usage".
</p>
<ul>
<li>
Usage:<br> config ecn \[OPTIONS\]
</li>
</ul>
<pre><code>  ECN Config OPTIONS:
    -profile &lt;profile_name&gt;       Profile name  [required] - Even though the profile_name is specified as optional parameter, it is a mandatory parameter.
    -rmax &lt;red threshold max&gt;     Set red max threshold
    -rmin &lt;red threshold min&gt;     Set red min threshold
    -ymax &lt;yellow threshold max&gt;  Set yellow max threshold
    -ymin &lt;yellow threshold min&gt;  Set yellow min threshold
    -gmax &lt;green threshold max&gt;   Set green max threshold
    -gmin &lt;green threshold min&gt;   Set green min threshold
    -v, --verbose                 Enable verbose output
    --help                        Show this message and exit.
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Example:
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config ecn -profile wredprofileabcd -rmax 100
   This command configures the "red max threshold" for the WRED profile name "wredprofileabcd". It will create the WRED profile if it does not exist.
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#ECN-Configuration-And-Show-Commands">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-interface-configuration-and-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#interface-configuration-and-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Interface
Configuration And Show-Commands
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-interface-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#interface-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Interface
Show Commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section lists all the possible show commands for the interfaces
available in the device. Following example gives the list of possible
shows on interfaces. Subsequent pages explain each of these commands in
detail.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
Example:
<pre><code>user@debug:~$ show interfaces -?

Show details of the network interfaces

Options:
  -?, -h, --help  Show this message and exit.

Commands:
counters     Show interface counters
description  Show interface status, protocol and...
naming_mode  Show interface naming_mode status
neighbor     Show neighbor related information
portchannel  Show PortChannel information
status       Show Interface status information
transceiver  Show SFP Transceiver information
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces counters</strong>
</p>
<p>
This show command displays packet counters for all interfaces since the
last time the counters were cleared. There is no facility to display
counters for one specific interface. Optional argument "-a" does not
have any significance in this command. Optional argument "-c" can be
used to clear the counters for all interfaces. Optional argument "-p"
specify a period (in seconds) with which to gather counters over.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces counters \[OPTIONS\]<br> OPTIONS:<br> -a,
--printall<br> -c, --clear<br> -p, --period TEXT
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces counters
      IFACE    STATE            RX_OK       RX_BPS    RX_UTIL    RX_ERR    RX_DRP    RX_OVR            TX_OK       TX_BPS    TX_UTIL    TX_ERR    TX_DRP    TX_OVR
-----------  -------  ---------------  -----------  ---------  --------  --------  --------  ---------------  -----------  ---------  --------  --------  --------
  Ethernet0        U  471,729,839,997  653.87 MB/s     12.77%         0    18,682         0  409,682,385,925  556.84 MB/s     10.88%         0         0         0
  Ethernet4        U  453,838,006,636  632.97 MB/s     12.36%         0     1,636         0  388,299,875,056  529.34 MB/s     10.34%         0         0         0
  Ethernet8        U  549,034,764,539  761.15 MB/s     14.87%         0    18,274         0  457,603,227,659  615.20 MB/s     12.02%         0         0         0
 Ethernet12        U  458,052,204,029  636.84 MB/s     12.44%         0    17,614         0  388,341,776,615  527.37 MB/s     10.30%         0         0         0
 Ethernet16        U   16,679,692,972   13.83 MB/s      0.27%         0    17,605         0   18,206,586,265   17.51 MB/s      0.34%         0         0         0
 Ethernet20        U   47,983,339,172   35.89 MB/s      0.70%         0     2,174         0   58,986,354,359   51.83 MB/s      1.01%         0         0         0
 Ethernet24        U   33,543,533,441   36.59 MB/s      0.71%         0     1,613         0   43,066,076,370   49.92 MB/s      0.97%         0         0         0
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Optionally, you can specify a period (in seconds) with which to gather
counters over. Note that this function will take <code>\<period\></code>
seconds to execute.
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces counters -p 5
      IFACE    STATE    RX_OK       RX_BPS    RX_UTIL    RX_ERR    RX_DRP    RX_OVR    TX_OK       TX_BPS    TX_UTIL    TX_ERR    TX_DRP    TX_OVR
-----------  -------  -------  -----------  ---------  --------  --------  --------  -------  -----------  ---------  --------  --------  --------
Ethernet0         U      515   59.14 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0    1,305  127.60 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0
Ethernet4         U      305   26.54 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0      279   39.12 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0
Ethernet8         U      437   42.96 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0      182   18.37 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0
Ethernet12        U      284   40.79 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0      160   13.03 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0
Ethernet16        U      377   32.64 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0      214   18.01 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0
Ethernet20        U      284   36.81 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0      138  8758.25 B/s      0.00%         0         0         0
Ethernet24        U      173   16.09 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0      169   11.39 KB/s      0.00%         0         0         0
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces description</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the key fields of the interfaces such as
Operational Status, Administrative Status, Alias and Description.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces description \[INTERFACENAME\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces description
Interface    Oper    Admin            Alias           Description
-----------  ------  -------  ---------------  --------------------
Ethernet0    down       up   hundredGigE1/1  T0-1:hundredGigE1/30
Ethernet4    down       up   hundredGigE1/2  T0-2:hundredGigE1/30
Ethernet8    down     down   hundredGigE1/3        hundredGigE1/3
Ethernet12    down     down   hundredGigE1/4        hundredGigE1/4
</code></pre>
<pre><code>show the description for one particular interface.
admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces description Ethernet4
Interface    Oper    Admin           Alias           Description
-----------  ------  -------  --------------  --------------------
Ethernet4    down       up  hundredGigE1/2  T0-2:hundredGigE1/30

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces naming\_mode</strong>
</p>
<p>
Refer sub-section
<a href="#Interface-Naming-Mode">Interface-Naming-Mode</a>
</p>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces neighbor</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to display the list of expected neighbors for all
interfaces (or for a particular interface) that is configured.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces neighbor expected \[INTERFACENAME\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces neighbor expected
  LocalPort    Neighbor    NeighborPort     NeighborLoopback    NeighborMgmt    NeighborType
  -----------  ----------  ---------------  ------------------  --------------  --------------
  Ethernet0    T0-1        hundredGigE1/30  None                10.11.162.45    ToRRouter
  Ethernet4    T0-2        hundredGigE1/30  None                10.11.162.44    ToRRouter
  Ethernet112  T2-1        hundredGigE1/2   None                10.11.150.201   SpineRouter
  Ethernet116  T2-2        hundredGigE1/2   None                10.11.150.202   SpineRouter
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces portchannel</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays information regarding port-channel interfaces
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces portchannel
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces portchannel
Flags: A - active, I - inactive, Up - up, Dw - Down, N/A - not available, S - selected, D - deselected
  No.  Team Dev       Protocol     Ports
-----  -------------  -----------  ---------------------------
   24  PortChannel24  LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet28(S) Ethernet24(S)
   48  PortChannel48  LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet52(S) Ethernet48(S)
   40  PortChannel40  LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet44(S) Ethernet40(S)
    0  PortChannel0   LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet0(S) Ethernet4(S)
    8  PortChannel8   LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet8(S) Ethernet12(S)
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show interface status</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays some more fields such as Lanes, Speed, MTU, Type,
Asymmetric PFC status and also the operational and administrative status
of the interfaces
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces status \[INTERFACENAME\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>show interface status of all interfaces

admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces status
Interface            Lanes    Speed    MTU            Alias    Oper    Admin    Type    Asym PFC
-----------  ---------------  -------  -----  ---------------  ------  -------  ------  ----------
Ethernet0      49,50,51,52     100G   9100   hundredGigE1/1    down       up     N/A         off
Ethernet4      53,54,55,56     100G   9100   hundredGigE1/2    down       up     N/A         off
Ethernet8      57,58,59,60     100G   9100   hundredGigE1/3    down     down     N/A         off
&lt;contiues to display all the interfaces&gt;

</code></pre>
<pre><code>show interface status for one particular interface

admin@sonic:~$ show interface status Ethernet0
Interface     Lanes    Speed    MTU            Alias    Oper    Admin
-----------  --------  -------  -----   --------------  ------  -------
Ethernet0   101,102      40G   9100   fortyGigE1/1/1      up       up

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces transceiver</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is already explained <a href="#Transceivers">here</a>
</p>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-interface-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#interface-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Interface
Config Commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains the following list of configuration on the
interfaces.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
ip - To add or remove IP address for the interface
</li>
<li>
pfc - to set the PFC configuration for the interface
</li>
<li>
shutdown - to administratively shut down the interface
</li>
<li>
speed - to set the interface speed
</li>
<li>
startup - to bring up the administratively shutdown interface
</li>
</ol>
<p>
<strong>config interface ip add/remove</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used for adding or removing the IP address for an
interface. IP address for either physical interface or for portchannel
or for VLAN interface can be configured using this command.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config interface ip add \<ip\_addr\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Examples:
</p>
<p>
<strong>Adding IP Address</strong>
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface Vlan100 ip add 10.11.12.13/24
</code></pre>
<p>
<strong>Removing IP Address</strong>
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface Vlan100 ip remove 10.11.12.13/24
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config interface pfc</strong><br> This command is used for
setting the asymmetric PFC for an interface to either "on" or "off".
Once if it is configured, use "show interfaces status" to check the
same.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config interface pfc asymmetric on/off
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Examples:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface Ethernet0 pfc asymmetric on
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config interface shutdown</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to administratively shut down either the Physical
interface or port channel interface. Once if it is configured, use "show
interfaces status" to check the same.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config interface shutdown
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface Ethernet0 shutdown
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config interface startup</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used for administratively bringing up the Physical
interface or port channel interface.Once if it is configured, use "show
interfaces status" to check the same.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config interface startup
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface Ethernet0 startup
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config interface speed</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to configure the speed for the Physical interface.
Use the value 40000 for setting it to 40G and 100000 for 100G. Users
need to know the device to configure it properly. Dynamic breakout
feature is yet supported in SONiC and hence uses cannot configure any
values other than 40G and 100G.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config interface speed
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface Ethernet0 speed 40000
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#Interface-Configuration-And-Show-Commands">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-interface-naming-mode" class="anchor" href="#interface-naming-mode" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Interface
Naming Mode
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-interface-naming-mode-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#interface-naming-mode-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Interface
naming mode show commands
</h2>
<p>
This command displays the current interface naming mode. Interface
naming mode originally set to 'default'. Interfaces are referenced by
default SONiC interface names. Users can change the naming\_mode using
"config interface\_naming\_mode" command.
</p>
<p>
<strong>show interfce naming mode</strong><br> This command displays the
current interface naming mode
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces naming\_mode
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces naming_mode
**default**
- "default" is the name of the default naming_mode since users have not modified it in this example.

Following example shows the modified interface_naming_mode
admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces naming_mode
**alias**
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-interface-naming-mode-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#interface-naming-mode-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Interface
naming mode config commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>config interface naming mode</strong><br> This command is used
to change the interface naming mode. Users can select between default
mode (SONiC interface names) or alias mode (Hardware vendor names). The
user must log out and log back in for changes to take effect. Note that
the newly-applied interface mode will affect all interface-related
show/config commands.
</p>
<p>
NOTE: Some platforms do not support alias mapping. In such cases, this
command is not applicable. Such platforms always use the same SONiC
interface names.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config interface\_naming\_mode (default \| alias)
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Interface naming mode originally set to 'default'. Interfaces are
referenced by default SONiC interface names:
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces naming_mode
  default

  admin@sonic:~$ show interface status Ethernet0
    Interface     Lanes    Speed    MTU            Alias    Oper    Admin
  -----------  --------  -------  -----   --------------  ------  -------
    Ethernet0   101,102      40G   9100   fortyGigE1/1/1      up       up

  admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface_naming_mode alias
  Please logout and log back in for changes take effect.
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
After user logs out and back in again, interfaces now referenced by
hardware vendor aliases:
</li>
</ul>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces naming_mode
  alias

  admin@sonic:~$ sudo config interface fortyGigE1/1/1 shutdown
  admin@sonic:~$ show interface status fortyGigE1/1/1
    Interface     Lanes    Speed    MTU            Alias    Oper    Admin
  -----------  --------  -------  -----   --------------  ------  -------
    Ethernet0   101,102      40G   9100   fortyGigE1/1/1    down     down
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or <a href="#Interface-Naming-Mode">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-ip" class="anchor" href="#ip" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>IP
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-ip-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#ip-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>IP
show commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains the various IP protocol specific show commands
that are used to display the following.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
routes
</li>
<li>
bgp details - Explained in the <a href="#show-bgp">bgp section</a>
</li>
<li>
IP interfaces
</li>
<li>
prefix-list
</li>
<li>
protocol
</li>
</ol>
<p>
<strong>show ip route</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays either all the route entries from the routing
table or a specific route.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ip route \[\]\`
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ip route
Codes: K - kernel route, C - connected, S - static, R - RIP,
       O - OSPF, I - IS-IS, B - BGP, P - PIM, A - Babel,
       &gt; - selected route, * - FIB route
  S&gt;* 0.0.0.0/0 [200/0] via 10.11.162.254, eth0
  C&gt;* 1.1.0.0/16 is directly connected, Vlan100
  C&gt;* 10.1.0.1/32 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* 10.1.0.32/32 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* 10.1.1.0/31 is directly connected, Ethernet112
  C&gt;* 10.1.1.2/31 is directly connected, Ethernet116
  C&gt;* 10.11.162.0/24 is directly connected, eth0
  C&gt;* 10.12.0.102/32 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* 127.0.0.0/8 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* 240.127.1.0/24 is directly connected, docker0

</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Optionally, you can specify an IP address in order to display only
routes to that particular IP address
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show ip route 10.1.1.0
  Routing entry for 10.1.1.0/31
    Known via "connected", distance 0, metric 0, best
    * directly connected, Ethernet112
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ip interfaces</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the details about all the Layer3 IP interfaces in
the device for which IP address has been assigned. The type of
interfaces include the following.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
Front panel physical ports.
</li>
<li>
PortChannel.
</li>
<li>
VLAN interface.
</li>
<li>
Loopback interfaces
</li>
<li>
docker interface and
</li>
<li>
management interface
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ip interfaces
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show ip interfaces
  Interface        IPv4 address/mask    Admin/Oper
  ---------------  -------------------  ------------
  Ethernet112      10.1.1.0/31          up/up
  Ethernet116      10.1.1.2/31          up/up
  PortChannel0001  10.0.1.1/31          up/down
  PortChannel0002  10.0.1.3/31          up/down
  Vlan100          1.1.2.2/16           up/down
  docker0          240.127.1.1/24       up/down
  eth0             10.11.162.42/24      up/up
  lo               127.0.0.1/8          up/up
                 10.1.0.1/32
                 10.1.0.32/32
                 10.12.0.102/32
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ip protocol</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the route-map that is configured for the routing
protocol. Refer the routing stack
<a href="https://www.quagga.net/docs/quagga.pdf" rel="nofollow">Quagga
Command Reference</a> or
<a href="https://buildmedia.readthedocs.org/media/pdf/frrouting/latest/frrouting.pdf" rel="nofollow">FRR
Command Reference</a> to know more about this command.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ip protocol
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  show ip protocol
  Protocol    : route-map
  ------------------------
  system      : none
  kernel      : none
  connected   : none
  static      : none
  rip         : none
  ripng       : none
  ospf        : none
  ospf6       : none
  isis        : none
  bgp         : RM_SET_SRC
  pim         : none
  hsls        : none
  olsr        : none
  babel       : none
  any         : none
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-ipv6-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#ipv6-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>IPv6
show commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains the various IPv6 protocol specific show
commands that are used to display the following.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
routes
</li>
<li>
IPv6 bgp details - Explained in the <a href="#show-bgp">bgp section</a>
</li>
<li>
IP interfaces
</li>
<li>
protocol
</li>
</ol>
<p>
<strong>show ipv6 route</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays either all the IPv6 route entries from the routing
table or a specific IPv6 route.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ipv6 route \[\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 route
  Codes: K - kernel route, C - connected, S - static, R - RIPng,
       O - OSPFv6, I - IS-IS, B - BGP, A - Babel,
       &gt; - selected route, * - FIB route

  C&gt;* ::1/128 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* 2018:2001::/126 is directly connected, Ethernet112
  C&gt;* 2018:2002::/126 is directly connected, Ethernet116
  C&gt;* fc00:1::32/128 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* fc00:1::102/128 is directly connected, lo
  C&gt;* fc00:2::102/128 is directly connected, eth0
  C * fe80::/64 is directly connected, Vlan100
  C * fe80::/64 is directly connected, Ethernet112
  C * fe80::/64 is directly connected, Ethernet116
  C * fe80::/64 is directly connected, Bridge
  C * fe80::/64 is directly connected, PortChannel0011
  C&gt;* fe80::/64 is directly connected, eth0

</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Optionally, you can specify an IPv6 address in order to display only
routes to that particular IPv6 address
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 route  fc00:1::32
  Routing entry for fc00:1::32/128
    Known via "connected", distance 0, metric 0, best
    * directly connected, lo
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ipv6 interfaces</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the details about all the Layer3 IPv6 interfaces
in the device for which IPv6 address has been assigned. The type of
interfaces include the following.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
Front panel physical ports.
</li>
<li>
PortChannel.
</li>
<li>
VLAN interface.
</li>
<li>
Loopback interfaces
</li>
<li>
management interface
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ipv6 interfaces
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show ipv6 interfaces
  Interface        IPv6 address/mask                            Admin/Oper
  ---------------  -------------------------------------------  ------------
  Bridge           fe80::d494:dcff:fe37:535e%Bridge/64          up/down
  Ethernet112      2018:2001::1/126                             up/up
                 fe80::3617:ebff:fe38:100%Ethernet112/64
  Ethernet116      2018:2002::1/126                             up/up
                 fe80::3617:ebff:fe38:100%Ethernet116/64
  PortChannel0001  2018:1002::2/126                             up/down
  PortChannel0002  2018:1002::6/126                             up/down
  PortChannel0011  fe80::3617:ebff:fe38:100%PortChannel0011/64  up/up
  Vlan100          fe80::3617:ebff:fe38:100%Vlan100/64          up/down
  eth0             fc00:2::102/128                              up/up
                 fe80::3617:ebff:fe38:100%eth0/64
  lo               fc00:1::102/128                              up/up
                 fc00:1::32/128
                 ::1/128

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show ipv6 protocol</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the route-map that is configured for the IPv6
routing protocol. Refer the routing stack
<a href="https://www.quagga.net/docs/quagga.pdf" rel="nofollow">Quagga
Command Reference</a> or
<a href="https://buildmedia.readthedocs.org/media/pdf/frrouting/latest/frrouting.pdf" rel="nofollow">FRR
Command Reference</a> to know more about this command.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show ipv6 protocol
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  show ipv6 protocol
  Protocol    : route-map
  ------------------------
  system      : none
  kernel      : none
  connected   : none
  static      : none
  rip         : none
  ripng       : none
  ospf        : none
  ospf6       : none
  isis        : none
  bgp         : RM_SET_SRC6
  pim         : none
  hsls        : none
  olsr        : none
  babel       : none
  any         : none
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or <a href="#IP">Beginning of this section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-lldp" class="anchor" href="#lldp" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>LLDP
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-lldp-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#lldp-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>LLDP
show commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show lldp table</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the brief summary of all LLDP neighbors.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show lldp table\`
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show lldp table
  Capability codes: (R) Router, (B) Bridge, (O) Other
  LocalPort    RemoteDevice       RemotePortID         Capability    RemotePortDescr
  -----------  -----------------  -------------------  ------------  --------------------
  Ethernet112  T1-1               hundredGigE1/2       BR            T0-2:hundredGigE1/29
  Ethernet116  T1-2               hundredGigE1/2       BR            T0-2:hundredGigE1/30
  eth0         swtor-b2lab2-1610  GigabitEthernet 0/2  OBR
  --------------------------------------------------
  Total entries displayed:  3
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>

</p>

</li>
