<h1>
<a id="user-content-loading-reloading-and-saving-configuration" class="anchor" href="#loading-reloading-and-saving-configuration" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Loading,
Reloading And Saving Configuration
</h1>
<p>
This section explains the commands that are used to load the
configuration from either the ConfigDB or from the minigraph.
</p>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-load-config-command" class="anchor" href="#load-config-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Load
config command
</h2>
<p>
This command is used to load the configuration from configDB. This
command loads the configuration from the input file (if user specifies
this optional filename, it will use that input file. Or else, it will
use the /etc/sonic/config\_db.json as the input file) into CONFIG\_DB.
The configurations present in the input file are applied on top of the
already running configuration. This command does not flush the config DB
before loading the new configuration. i.e.┬áIf the configuration present
in the input file is same as the current running-configuration, nothing
happens. If the config present in the input file is not present in
running-configuration, it will be added. If the config present in the
input file matches (when key matches) with the running-configuration, it
will be modified as per the new values for those keys.
</p>
<p>
When user specifies the optional argument "-y" or "--yes", this command
forces the loading without prompting the user for confirmation. If the
argument is not specified, it prompts the user to confirm whether user
really wants to load this configuration file.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config load \[OPTIONS\] \[FILENAME\] OPTIONS : -y, --yes
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config load
 Load config from the file /etc/sonic/config_db.json? [y/N]: y
 Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -j /etc/sonic/config_db.json --write-to-db
 root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-load_mgmt_config-command" class="anchor" href="#load_mgmt_config-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Load\_mgmt\_config
command
</h2>
<p>
This command is used to reconfigure hostname and mgmt interface based on
device description file. This command either uses the optional file
specified as arguement or looks for the file
"/etc/sonic/device\_desc.xml". If the file does not exist or if the file
does not have valid fields for "hostname" and "ManagementAddress", it
fails.
</p>
<p>
When user specifies the optional argument "-y" or "--yes", this command
forces the loading without prompting the user for confirmation. If the
argument is not specified, it prompts the user to confirm whether user
really wants to load this configuration file.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config load\_mgmt\_config \[OPTIONS\] \[FILENAME\] OPTIONS :
-y, --yes
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config load_mgmt_config
 Reload config from minigraph? [y/N]: y
 Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -M /etc/sonic/device_desc.xml --write-to-db
 root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-load_minigraph-config-command" class="anchor" href="#load_minigraph-config-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Load\_minigraph
config command
</h2>
<p>
This command is used to load the configuration from
/etc/sonic/minigraph.xml. When users do not want to use configuration
from config\_db.json, they can copy the minigraph.xml configuration file
to the device and load it using this command. This command restarts
various services running in the device and it takes some time to
complete the command. NOTE: If the user had logged in using SSH, users
might get disconnected and some configuration failures might happen
which might be hard to recover. Users need to reconnect their SSH
sessions after configuring the management IP address. It is recommended
to execute this command from console port. NOTE: Management interface IP
address and default route (or specific route) may require
reconfiguration in case if those parameters are not part of the
minigraph.xml.
</p>
<p>
When user specifies the optional argument "-y" or "--yes", this command
forces the loading without prompting the user for confirmation. If the
argument is not specified, it prompts the user to confirm whether user
really wants to load this configuration file.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config load\_minigraph \[OPTIONS\] OPTIONS : -y, --yes
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config load_minigraph
 Reload config from minigraph? [y/N]: y
 Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -j /etc/sonic/config_db.json --write-to-db
 root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-reload-config-command" class="anchor" href="#reload-config-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Reload
config command
</h2>
<p>
This command is used to clear current configuration and import new
configurationn from the input file or from /etc/sonic/config\_db.json.
This command shall stop all services before clearing the configuration
and it then restarts those services.
</p>
<p>
This command restarts various services running in the device and it
takes some time to complete the command. NOTE: If the user had logged in
using SSH, users <strong>might get disconnected</strong> depending upon
the new management IP address. Users need to reconnect their SSH
sessions. In general, it is recommended to execute this command from
console port after disconnecting all SSH sessions to the device. When
users to do "config reload" the newly loaded config may have management
IP address, or it may not have management IP address. If mgmtIP is there
in the newly loaded config file, that mgmtIP might be same as previously
configured value or it might be different. This difference in mgmtIP
address values results in following possible behaviours.
</p>
<p>
Case1: Previously configured mgmtIP is same as newly loaded mgmtIP. The
SSH session may not be affected at all, but it's possible that there
will be a brief interruption in the SSH session. But, assuming the
client's timeout value isn't on the order of a couple of seconds, the
session would most likely just resume again as soon as the interface is
reconfigured and up with the same IP. Case2: Previously configured
mgmtIP is different from newly loaded mgmtIP. Users will lose their SSH
connections. Case3: Newly loaded config does not have any mgmtIP. Users
will lose their SSH connections.
</p>
<p>
NOTE: Management interface IP address and default route (or specific
route) may require reconfiguration in case if those parameters are not
part of the minigraph.xml.
</p>
<p>
When user specifies the optional argument "-y" or "--yes", this command
forces the loading without prompting the user for confirmation. If the
argument is not specified, it prompts the user to confirm whether user
really wants to load this configuration file.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config reload \[-y\|--yes\] \[-l \| --load-sysinfo\]
\[FILENAME\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config reload
 Clear current config and reload config from the file /etc/sonic/config_db.json? [y/N]: y
 Running command: systemctl stop dhcp_relay
 Running command: systemctl stop swss
 Running command: systemctl stop snmp
 Warning: Stopping snmp.service, but it can still be activated by:
   snmp.timer
 Running command: systemctl stop lldp
 Running command: systemctl stop pmon
 Running command: systemctl stop bgp
 Running command: systemctl stop teamd
 Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -H -k Force10-Z9100-C32 --write-to-db
 Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -j /etc/sonic/config_db.json --write-to-db
 Running command: systemctl restart hostname-config
 Running command: systemctl restart interfaces-config
 Timeout, server 10.11.162.42 not responding.
 root@T1-2:~#
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-save-config--command" class="anchor" href="#save-config--command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Save
config command
</h2>
<p>
This command is to save the config DB configuration into the
user-specified filename or into the default /etc/sonic/config\_db.json.
This saves the configuration into the disk which is available even after
reboots. Saved file can be transferred to remote machines for debugging.
If users wants to load the configuration from this new file at any point
of time, they can use "config load" command and provide this newly
generated file as input. If users wants this newly generated file to be
used during reboot, they need to copy this file to
/etc/sonic/config\_db.json.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config save \[OPTIONS\] \[FILENAME\] OPTIONS : -y, --yes
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>root@T1-2:~# config save -y /etc/sonic/config2.json - this saves to the filename specified.
root@T1-2:~# config save -y - this saves to /etc/sonic/config_db.json.
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#loading-reloading-and-saving-configuration">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-mirroring-configuration-and-show" class="anchor" href="#mirroring-configuration-and-show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Mirroring
Configuration And Show
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-mirroring-show-command" class="anchor" href="#mirroring-show-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Mirroring
Show command
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show mirror\_session</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the mirror sessions that are configured.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show mirror\_session
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show mirror session
Name       Status    SRC IP     DST IP    GRE    DSCP    TTL    Queue
---------  --------  ---------  --------  -----  ------  -----  -------
everflow0  active    10.1.0.32  10.0.0.7

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-mirroring-config-command" class="anchor" href="#mirroring-config-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Mirroring
Config command
</h2>
<p>
This command is used to add or remove mirroring sessions. Mirror session
is identified by "session\_name". While adding a new session, users need
to configure the following fields that are used while forwarding the
mirrored packets.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
source IP address,
</li>
<li>
destination IP address,
</li>
<li>
DSCP (QoS) value with which mirrored packets are forwarded
</li>
<li>
TTL value
</li>
<li>
optional - GRE Type in case if user wants to send the packet via GRE
tunnel. GRE type could be anything; it could also be left as empty; by
default, it is 0x8949 for Mellanox; and 0x88be for the rest of the
chips.
</li>
<li>
optional - Queue in which packets shall be sent out of the device. Valid
values 0 to 7 for most of the devices. Users need to know their device
and the number of queues supported in that device.
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config mirror\_session add \<session\_name\> \<src\_ip\>
\<dst\_ip\><br> \[gre\_type\] \[queue\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  root@T1-2:~# config mirror_session add mrr_abcd 1.2.3.4 20.21.22.23 8 100 0x6558 0
  root@T1-2:~# show mirror_session
  Name       Status    SRC IP       DST IP       GRE     DSCP    TTL    Queue
  ---------  --------  -----------  -----------  ------  ------  -----  -------
  mrr_abcd   inactive  1.2.3.4      20.21.22.23  0x6558  8       100    0
  root@T1-2:~#

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#Mirroring-Configuration-And-Show">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-ntp" class="anchor" href="#ntp" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>NTP
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-ntp-show-command" class="anchor" href="#ntp-show-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>NTP
show command

</p>

This command displays a list of NTP peers known to the server as well as
a summary of their state.

Usage:<br> show ntp

     remote           refid      st t when poll reach   delay   offset  jitter

  *204.2.134.164   46.233.231.73    2 u  916 1024  377    3.079    0.394   0.128
</code></pre>

<h1>
<a id="user-content-platform-specific-commands" class="anchor" href="#platform-specific-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Platform
Specific Commands
</h1>
<p>
<strong>config platform mlnx</strong><br> This command is valid only on
mellanox devices. The sub-commands for "config platform" gets populated
only on mellanox platforms. There are no other subcommands on
non-Mellanox devices and hence this command appears empty and useless in
other platforms. Mellanox specific commands shall be filled in later.
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-portchannel-configuration-and-show" class="anchor" href="#portchannel-configuration-and-show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>PortChannel
Configuration And Show
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-portchannel-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#portchannel-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>PortChannel
Show commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show interfaces portchannel</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the port channels that are configured in the
device and its current status.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show interfaces portchannel
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show interfaces portchannel
Flags: A - active, I - inactive, Up - up, Dw - Down, N/A - not available, S - selected, D - deselected
  No.  Team Dev       Protocol     Ports
-----  -------------  -----------  ---------------------------
   24  PortChannel24  LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet28(S) Ethernet24(S)
   48  PortChannel48  LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet52(S) Ethernet48(S)
   40  PortChannel40  LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet44(S) Ethernet40(S)
    0  PortChannel0   LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet0(S) Ethernet4(S)
    8  PortChannel8   LACP(A)(Up)  Ethernet8(S) Ethernet12(S)
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-portchannel-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#portchannel-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>PortChannel
Config commands
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains how to configure the portchannel and its
member ports.
</p>
<p>
<strong>config portchannel add/del \<portchannel\_name\></strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to add or delete the portchannel.<br> It is
recommended to use portchannel names in the format "PortChannelxxxx",
where "xxxx" is number of 1 to 4 digits. Ex: "PortChannel0002".
</p>
<p>
NOTE: If users specify any other name like "pc99", command will succeed,
but such names are not supported. Such names are not printed properly in
the "show interface portchannel" command. It is recommended not to use
such names.
</p>
<p>
When any port is already member of any other portchannel and if user
tries to add the same port in some other portchannel (without deleting
it from the current portchannel), the command fails internally. But, it
does not print any error message. In such cases, remove the member from
current portchannel and then add it to new portchannel.
</p>
<p>
Command takes two optional arguements given below.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
min-links - minimum number of links required to bring up the portchannel
</li>
<li>
fallback - true/false. LACP fallback feature can be enabled / disabled.
When it is set to true, only one member port will be selected as active
per portchannel during fallback mode. Refer
<a href="https://github.com/Azure/SONiC/blob/master/doc/lag/LACP%20Fallback%20Feature%20for%20SONiC_v0.5.md">https://github.com/Azure/SONiC/blob/master/doc/lag/LACP%20Fallback%20Feature%20for%20SONiC\_v0.5.md</a>
for more details about fallback feature.
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config portchannel add/del \<portchannel\_name\> \[min-links
INTEGER\] \[fallback true/false\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config portchannel add PortChannel0011
This command will create the portchannel with name "PortChannel0011".
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config portchannel member add/del \<portchannel\_name\>
\<member\_portname\></strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is to add or delete a member port into the already created
portchannel.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config portchannel member add/del \<portchannel\_name\>
\<member\_portname\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config portchannel member add PortChannel0011 Ethernet4
This command will add Ethernet4 as member of the portchannel "PortChannel0011".
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or
<a href="#PortChannel-Configuration-And-Show">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-qos-configuration--show" class="anchor" href="#qos-configuration--show" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>QoS
Configuration & Show
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-qos-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#qos-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>QoS
Show commands
</h2>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-pfc" class="anchor" href="#pfc" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>PFC
</h3>
<p>
<strong>show pfc counters</strong><br> This command displays the details
of Rx & Tx priority-flow-control (pfc) for all ports. This command can
be used to clear the counters using -c option.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show pfc counters \[-c or --clear\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show pfc counters
   Port Rx    PFC0    PFC1    PFC2    PFC3    PFC4    PFC5    PFC6    PFC7
 -----------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------
 Ethernet0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
 Ethernet4       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
 Ethernet8       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
Ethernet12       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0

   Port Tx    PFC0    PFC1    PFC2    PFC3    PFC4    PFC5    PFC6    PFC7
 -----------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------  ------
 Ethernet0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
 Ethernet4       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
 Ethernet8       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
Ethernet12       0       0       0       0       0       0       0       0
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-queue-and-priority-group" class="anchor" href="#queue-and-priority-group" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Queue
And Priority-Group
</h3>
<p>
This sub-section explains the following queue parameters that can be
displayed using "show queue" command.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
queue counters
</li>
<li>
queue watermark
</li>
<li>
priority-group watermark
</li>
<li>
queue persistent-watermark
</li>
</ol>
<p>
<strong>show queue counters</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays packet and byte counters for all queues of all
ports or one specific-port given as arguement. This command can be used
to clear the counters for all queues of all ports. Note that port
specific clear is not supported.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show queue counters \[-c or --clear\] \[\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  This example gives the sample output from two ports Ethernet0 and Ethernet4.

  admin@sonic:~$ show queue counters
       Port    TxQ    Counter/pkts    Counter/bytes    Drop/pkts    Drop/bytes
  ---------  -----  --------------  ---------------  -----------  ------------
  Ethernet0    UC0               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC1               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC2               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC3               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC4               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC5               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC6               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC7               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC8               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    UC9               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC0               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC1               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC2               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC3               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC4               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC5               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC6               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC7               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC8               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet0    MC9               0                0            0             0

       Port    TxQ    Counter/pkts    Counter/bytes    Drop/pkts    Drop/bytes
  ---------  -----  --------------  ---------------  -----------  ------------
  Ethernet4    UC0               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC1               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC2               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC3               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC4               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC5               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC6               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC7               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC8               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    UC9               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC0               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC1               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC2               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC3               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC4               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC5               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC6               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC7               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC8               0                0            0             0
  Ethernet4    MC9               0                0            0             0
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Optionally, you can specify an interface name in order to display only
that particular interface
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show queue counters Ethernet72
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show queue watermark</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the user watermark for the queues (Egress shared
pool occupancy per queue) for either the unicast queues or multicast
queues for all ports
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show queue watermark \<multicast\|unicast\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show queue  watermark unicast
Egress shared pool occupancy per unicast queue:
       Port    UC0    UC1    UC2    UC3    UC4    UC5    UC6    UC7
-----------  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----
  Ethernet0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0
  Ethernet4      0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0
  Ethernet8      0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0
  Ethernet12     0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0

admin@sonic:~$ show queue  watermark multicast (Egress shared pool occupancy per multicast queue)

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show priority-group watermark\|persistent-watermark</strong><br>
This command displays the user watermark or persistent-watermark for the
Ingress "headroom" or "shared pool occupancy" per priority-group for all
ports
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show priority-group \<watermark\|persistent-watermark\>
\<headroom\|shared\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show priority-group  watermark shared
Ingress shared pool occupancy per PG:
       Port    PG0    PG1    PG2    PG3    PG4    PG5    PG6    PG7
-----------  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----
  Ethernet0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0
  Ethernet4      0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0
  Ethernet8      0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0
  Ethernet12     0      0      0      0      0      0      0      0

admin@sonic:~$ show priority-group watermark headroom   (Ingress headroom per PG)
admin@sonic:~$ show priority-group persistent-watermark shared (Ingress shared pool occupancy per PG)
admin@sonic:~$ show priority-group persistent-watermark headroom (Ingress headroom per PG)
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
In addition to user watermark("show queue\|priority-group watermark
..."), a persistent watermark is available. It hold values independently
of user watermark. This way user can use "user watermark" for debugging,
clear it, etc, but the "persistent watermark" will not be affected.
</p>
<p>
<strong>show queue persistent-watermark</strong><br> This command
displays the user persistet-watermark for the queues (Egress shared pool
occupancy per queue) for either the unicast queues or multicast queues
for all ports
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show queue persistent-watermark \<unicast\|multicast\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show queue persistent-watermark unicast
Egress shared pool occupancy per unicast queue:
       Port    UC0    UC1    UC2    UC3    UC4    UC5    UC6    UC7
-----------  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----  -----
  Ethernet0    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A
  Ethernet4    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A
  Ethernet8    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A
  Ethernet12   N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A    N/A

admin@sonic:~$ show queue persistent-watermark multicast (Egress shared pool occupancy per multicast queue)

</code></pre>
<p>
Both "user watermark" and "persistent watermark" can be cleared by user:
</p>
<pre><code>root@sonic:~# sonic-clear queue persistent-watermark unicast

root@sonic:~# sonic-clear queue persistent-watermark multicast

root@sonic:~# sonic-clear priority-group persistent-watermark shared

root@sonic:~# sonic-clear priority-group persistent-watermark headroom
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-qos-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#qos-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>QoS
config commands
</h2>
<p>
<strong>config qos clear</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to clear all the QoS configuration from all the
following QOS Tables in ConfigDB.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
TC\_TO\_PRIORITY\_GROUP\_MAP,
</li>
<li>
MAP\_PFC\_PRIORITY\_TO\_QUEUE,
</li>
<li>
TC\_TO\_QUEUE\_MAP,
</li>
<li>
DSCP\_TO\_TC\_MAP,
</li>
<li>
SCHEDULER,
</li>
<li>
PFC\_PRIORITY\_TO\_PRIORITY\_GROUP\_MAP,
</li>
<li>
PORT\_QOS\_MAP,
</li>
<li>
WRED\_PROFILE,
</li>
<li>
QUEUE,
</li>
<li>
CABLE\_LENGTH,
</li>
<li>
BUFFER\_POOL,
</li>
<li>
BUFFER\_PROFILE,
</li>
<li>
BUFFER\_PG,
</li>
<li>
BUFFER\_QUEUE
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config qos clear
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config qos clear

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config qos reload</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to reload the QoS configuration. QoS configuration
has got two sets of configurations.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>
Generic QOS Configuration - This gives complete list of all possible QOS
configuration. Its given in the file
/usr/share/sonic/templates/qos\_config.j2 in the device. Reference:
<a href="https://github.com/Azure/sonic-buildimage/blob/master/files/build_templates/qos_config.j2">https://github.com/Azure/sonic-buildimage/blob/master/files/build\_templates/qos\_config.j2</a>
Users have flexibility to have platform specific qos configuration by
placing the qos\_config.j2 file at /usr/share/sonic/device///. If users
want to modify any of this loaded QOS configuration, they can modify
this file in the device and then issue the "config qos reload" command.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Platform specific buffer configuration. Every platform has got platform
specific and topology specific (T0 or T1 or T2) buffer configuration at
/usr/share/sonic/device///buffers\_defaults\_tx.j2 In addition to
platform specific configuration file, a generic configuration file is
also present at /usr/share/sonic/templates/buffers\_config.j2.
Reference:
<a href="https://github.com/Azure/sonic-buildimage/blob/master/files/build_templates/buffers_config.j2">https://github.com/Azure/sonic-buildimage/blob/master/files/build\_templates/buffers\_config.j2</a>
Users can either modify the platform specific configuration file, or the
generic configuration file and then issue this "config qos reload"
command.
</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>
These configuration files are already loaded in the device as part of
the reboot process. In case if users wants to modify any of these
configurations, they need to modify the appropriate QOS tables and
fields in these files and then use this reload command. This command
uses those modified buffers.json.j2 file & qos.json.j2 file and reloads
the new QOS configuration. If users have not made any changes in these
configuration files, this command need not be executed.
</p>
<p>
Some of the example QOS configurations that users can modify are given
below.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
TC\_TO\_PRIORITY\_GROUP\_MAP
</li>
<li>
MAP\_PFC\_PRIORITY\_TO\_QUEUE
</li>
<li>
TC\_TO\_QUEUE\_MAP
</li>
<li>
DSCP\_TO\_TC\_MAP
</li>
<li>
SCHEDULER
</li>
<li>
PFC\_PRIORITY\_TO\_PRIORITY\_GROUP\_MAP
</li>
<li>
PORT\_QOS\_MAP
</li>
<li>
WRED\_PROFILE
</li>
<li>
CABLE\_LENGTH
</li>
<li>
BUFFER\_QUEUE
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config qos reload
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  root@T1-2:~# config qos reload
  Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -d -t /usr/share/sonic/device/x86_64-dell_z9100_c2538-r0/Force10-Z9100-C32/buffers.json.j2 &gt;/tmp/buffers.json
  Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -d -t /usr/share/sonic/device/x86_64-dell_z9100_c2538-r0/Force10-Z9100-C32/qos.json.j2 -y /etc/sonic/sonic_version.yml &gt;/tmp/qos.json
  Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -j /tmp/buffers.json --write-to-db
  Running command: /usr/local/bin/sonic-cfggen -j /tmp/qos.json --write-to-db
  root@T1-2:~#
  In this example, it uses the buffers.json.j2 file and qos.json.j2 file from platform specific folders.
  When there are no changes in the platform specific configutation files, they internally use the file "/usr/share/sonic/templates/buffers_config.j2" and "/usr/share/sonic/templates/qos_config.j2" to generate the configuration.
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or <a href="#QoS-Configuration-And-Show">Beginning of
this section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-startup--running-configuration" class="anchor" href="#startup--running-configuration" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Startup
& Running Configuration
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-startup-configuration-command" class="anchor" href="#startup-configuration-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Startup
Configuration command
</h2>
<p>
<strong>show startupconfiguration bgp</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to display the startup configuration for the BGP
module.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show startupconfiguration bgp\`
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@sonic:~$ show startupconfiguration bgp
  Routing-Stack is: quagga
  !
  ! =========== Managed by sonic-cfggen DO NOT edit manually! ====================
  ! generated by templates/quagga/bgpd.conf.j2 with config DB data
  ! file: bgpd.conf
  !
  !
  hostname T1-2
  password zebra
  log syslog informational
  log facility local4
  ! enable password !
  !
  ! bgp multiple-instance
  !
  route-map FROM_BGP_SPEAKER_V4 permit 10
  !
  route-map TO_BGP_SPEAKER_V4 deny 10
  !
  router bgp 65000
    bgp log-neighbor-changes
    bgp bestpath as-path multipath-relax
    no bgp default ipv4-unicast
    bgp graceful-restart restart-time 180

    &lt;Only the partial output is shown here. In actual command, more configuration information will be displayed&gt;
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-running-configuration-command" class="anchor" href="#running-configuration-command" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Running
Configuration command
</h2>
<p>
This sub-section explains the show commands for displaying the running
configuration for the following modules.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
bgp
</li>
<li>
interfaces
</li>
<li>
ntp
</li>
<li>
snmp
</li>
<li>
all
</li>
</ol>
<p>

</p>
<p>
This command displays the entire running configuration.
</p>
<ul>

<p>
Usage:<br> show runningconfiguration all
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>

</code></pre>

</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-system-state" class="anchor" href="#system-state" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>System
State
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-processes-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#processes-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Processes
show commands
</h2>
<p>
This command is used to determine the CPU utilization. It also lists the
active processes along with their corresponding process ID and other
relevant parameters.
</p>
<p>
This sub-section explains the various "processes" specific data that
includes the following.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
cpu Show processes CPU info
</li>
<li>
memory Show processes memory info
</li>
<li>
summary Show processes info
</li>
</ol>
<p>
"show processes" commands provide a wrapper over linux's "top" command.
"show process cpu" sorts the processes being displayed by
cpu-utilization, whereas "show process memory" does it attending to
processes' memory-utilization.
</p>
<p>
<strong>show processes cpu</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the current CPU usage by process. This command
uses linux's "top -bn 1 -o %CPU" command to display the output.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show processes cpu
</p>
<p>
Note that pipe option can be used using \" \| head -n\" to display only
the "n" number of lines.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@SONiC:~$ show processes cpu
top - 23:50:08 up  1:18,  1 user,  load average: 0.25, 0.29, 0.25
Tasks: 161 total,   1 running, 160 sleeping,   0 stopped,   0 zombie
%Cpu(s):  3.8 us,  1.0 sy,  0.0 ni, 95.1 id,  0.1 wa,  0.0 hi,  0.0 si,  0.0 st
KiB Mem:   8181216 total,  1161060 used,  7020156 free,   105656 buffers
KiB Swap:        0 total,        0 used,        0 free.   557560 cached Mem

  PID USER      PR  NI    VIRT    RES    SHR S  %CPU %MEM     TIME+ COMMAND
 2047 root      20   0  683772 109288  39652 S  23.8  1.3   7:44.79 syncd
 1351 root      20   0   43360   5616   2844 S  11.9  0.1   1:41.56 redis-server
10093 root      20   0   21944   2476   2088 R   5.9  0.0   0:00.03 top
    1 root      20   0   28992   5508   3236 S   0.0  0.1   0:06.42 systemd
    2 root      20   0       0      0      0 S   0.0  0.0   0:00.00 kthreadd
    3 root      20   0       0      0      0 S   0.0  0.0   0:00.56 ksoftirqd/0
    5 root       0 -20       0      0      0 S   0.0  0.0   0:00.00 kworker/0:0H
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show processes memory</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the current memory usage by processes. This
command uses linux's "top -bn 1 -o %MEM" command to display the output.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show processes memory
</p>
<p>
Note that pipe option can be used using \" \| head -n\" to display only
the "n" number of lines.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@SONiC:~$  show processes memory
  top - 23:41:24 up 7 days, 39 min,  2 users,  load average: 1.21, 1.19, 1.18
  Tasks: 191 total,   2 running, 189 sleeping,   0 stopped,   0 zombie
  %Cpu(s):  2.8 us, 20.7 sy,  0.0 ni, 76.3 id,  0.0 wa,  0.0 hi,  0.2 si,  0.0 st
  KiB Mem :  8162264 total,  5720412 free,   945516 used,  1496336 buff/cache
  KiB Swap:        0 total,        0 free,        0 used.  6855632 avail Mem

    PID USER      PR  NI    VIRT    RES    SHR S  %CPU %MEM     TIME+ COMMAND
  18051 root      20   0  851540 274784   8344 S   0.0  3.4   0:02.77 syncd
  17760 root      20   0 1293428 259212  58732 S   5.9  3.2  96:46.22 syncd
    508 root      20   0  725364  76244  38220 S   0.0  0.9   4:54.49 dockerd
  30853 root      20   0   96348  56824   7880 S   0.0  0.7   0:00.98 show
  17266 root      20   0  509876  49772  30640 S   0.0  0.6   0:06.36 docker
  24891 admin     20   0  515864  49560  30644 S   0.0  0.6   0:05.54 docker
  17643 admin     20   0  575668  49428  30628 S   0.0  0.6   0:06.29 docker
  23885 admin     20   0  369552  49344  30840 S   0.0  0.6   0:05.57 docker
  18055 root      20   0  509076  49260  30296 S   0.0  0.6   0:06.36 docker
  17268 root      20   0  371120  49052  30372 S   0.0  0.6   0:06.45 docker
   1227 root      20   0  443284  48640  30100 S   0.0  0.6   0:41.91 docker
  23785 admin     20   0  443796  48552  30128 S   0.0  0.6   0:05.58 docker
  17820 admin     20   0  435088  48144  29480 S   0.0  0.6   0:06.33 docker
    506 root      20   0 1151040  43140  23964 S   0.0  0.5   8:51.08 containerd
  18437 root      20   0   84852  26388   7380 S   0.0  0.3  65:59.76 python3.6
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show processes summary</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the current summary information about all the
processes
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show processes summary
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@SONiC:~$  show processes summary
    PID  PPID CMD                         %MEM %CPU
    1     0 /sbin/init                   0.0  0.0
    2     0 [kthreadd]                   0.0  0.0
    3     2 [ksoftirqd/0]                0.0  0.0
    5     2 [kworker/0:0H]               0.0  0.0
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-services--memory-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#services--memory-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>Services
& memory show commands
</h2>
<p>
These commands are used to know the services that are running and the
memory that is utilized currently.
</p>
<p>
<strong>show services</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the state of all the SONiC processes running
inside a docker container. This helps to identify the status of SONiC's
critical processes.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> sonic\_installer remove \<image\_name\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@lnos-x1-a-asw02:~$ show services
  dhcp_relay      docker
  ---------------------------
  UID        PID  PPID  C STIME TTY          TIME CMD
  root         1     0  0 05:26 ?        00:00:12 /usr/bin/python /usr/bin/supervi
  root        24     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:00 /usr/sbin/rsyslogd -n

  snmp    docker
  ---------------------------
  UID        PID  PPID  C STIME TTY          TIME CMD
  root         1     0  0 05:26 ?        00:00:16 /usr/bin/python /usr/bin/supervi
  root        24     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:02 /usr/sbin/rsyslogd -n
  Debian-+    29     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:04 /usr/sbin/snmpd -f -LS4d -u Debi
  root        31     1  1 05:26 ?        00:15:10 python3.6 -m sonic_ax_impl

  syncd   docker
  ---------------------------
  UID        PID  PPID  C STIME TTY          TIME CMD
  root         1     0  0 05:26 ?        00:00:13 /usr/bin/python /usr/bin/supervi
  root        12     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:00 /usr/sbin/rsyslogd -n
  root        17     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:00 /usr/bin/dsserve /usr/bin/syncd
  root        27    17 22 05:26 ?        04:09:30 /usr/bin/syncd --diag -p /usr/sh
  root        51    27  0 05:26 ?        00:00:01 /usr/bin/syncd --diag -p /usr/sh

  swss    docker
  ---------------------------
  UID        PID  PPID  C STIME TTY          TIME CMD
  root         1     0  0 05:26 ?        00:00:29 /usr/bin/python /usr/bin/supervi
  root        25     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:00 /usr/sbin/rsyslogd -n
  root        30     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:13 /usr/bin/orchagent -d /var/log/s
  root        42     1  1 05:26 ?        00:12:40 /usr/bin/portsyncd -p /usr/share
  root        45     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:00 /usr/bin/intfsyncd
  root        48     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:03 /usr/bin/neighsyncd
  root        59     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:01 /usr/bin/vlanmgrd
  root        92     1  0 05:26 ?        00:00:01 /usr/bin/intfmgrd
  root      3606     1  0 23:36 ?        00:00:00 bash -c /usr/bin/arp_update; sle
  root      3621  3606  0 23:36 ?        00:00:00 sleep 300
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show system-memory</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the system-wide memory utilization information --
just a wrapper over linux native "free" command
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> sonic\_installer remove \<image\_name\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@lnos-x1-a-asw02:~$ show system-memory
  Command: free -m -h
             total       used       free     shared    buffers     cached
  Mem:          3.9G       2.0G       1.8G        33M       324M       791M
  -/+ buffers/cache:       951M       2.9G
  Swap:           0B         0B         0B
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show mmu</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays virtual address to the physical address
translation status of the Memory Management Unit (MMU).
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show mmu
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>  admin@T1-2:~$ show mmu
  Pool: ingress_lossless_pool
  ----  --------
  xoff  4194112
  type  ingress
  mode  dynamic
  size  10875072
  ----  --------

  Pool: egress_lossless_pool
  ----  --------
  type  egress
  mode  static
  size  15982720
  ----  --------

  Pool: egress_lossy_pool
  ----  -------
  type  egress
  mode  dynamic
  size  9243812
  ----  -------

  Profile: egress_lossy_profile
  ----------  -------------------------------
  dynamic_th  3
  pool        [BUFFER_POOL|egress_lossy_pool]
  size        1518
  ----------  -------------------------------

  Profile: pg_lossless_100000_300m_profile
  ----------  -----------------------------------
  xon_offset  2288
  dynamic_th  -3
  xon         2288
  xoff        268736
  pool        [BUFFER_POOL|ingress_lossless_pool]
  size        1248
  ----------  -----------------------------------

  Profile: egress_lossless_profile
  ---------  ----------------------------------
  static_th  3995680
  pool       [BUFFER_POOL|egress_lossless_pool]
  size       1518
  ---------  ----------------------------------

  Profile: pg_lossless_100000_40m_profile
  ----------  -----------------------------------
  xon_offset  2288
  dynamic_th  -3
  xon         2288
  xoff        177632
  pool        [BUFFER_POOL|ingress_lossless_pool]
  size        1248
  ----------  -----------------------------------

  Profile: ingress_lossy_profile
  ----------  -----------------------------------
  dynamic_th  3
  pool        [BUFFER_POOL|ingress_lossless_pool]
  size        0
  ----------  -----------------------------------

  Profile: pg_lossless_40000_40m_profile
  ----------  -----------------------------------
  xon_offset  2288
  dynamic_th  -3
  xon         2288
  xoff        71552
  pool        [BUFFER_POOL|ingress_lossless_pool]
  size        1248
  ----------  -----------------------------------
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show line</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays serial port or a virtual network connection
status. This command is used only when SONiC is used as console switch.
This command is not applicable when SONiC used as regular switch. NOTE:
This command is not working. It crashes as follows. A bug ticket is
opened for this issue.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show line
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@T1-2:~$ show line

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
Go Back To <a href="#SONiC-COMMAND-LINE-INTERFACE-GUIDE">Beginning of
the document</a> or <a href="#System-State">Beginning of this
section</a>
</p>
<h1>
<a id="user-content-vlan--fdb" class="anchor" href="#vlan--fdb" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>VLAN
& FDB
</h1>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-vlan" class="anchor" href="#vlan" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>VLAN
</h2>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-vlan-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#vlan-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>VLAN
show commands
</h3>
<p>
<strong>show vlan brief</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays brief information about all the vlans configured
in the device. It displays the vlan ID, IP address (if configured for
the vlan), list of vlan member ports, whether the port is tagged or in
untagged mode and the DHCP Helper Address.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show vlan brief
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show vlan brief

  +-----------+--------------+-----------+----------------+-----------------------+
  |   VLAN ID | IP Address   | Ports     | Port Tagging   | DHCP Helper Address   |
  +===========+==============+===========+================+=======================+
  |       100 | 1.1.2.2/16   | Ethernet0 | tagged         | 192.0.0.1             |
  |           |              | Ethernet4 | tagged         | 192.0.0.2             |
  |           |              |           |                | 192.0.0.3             |
  +-----------+--------------+-----------+----------------+-----------------------+

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>show vlan config</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays all the vlan configuration.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show vlan config
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show vlan config
  Name       VID  Member     Mode
  -------  -----  ---------  ------
  Vlan100    100  Ethernet0  tagged
  Vlan100    100  Ethernet4  tagged

</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-vlan-config-commands" class="anchor" href="#vlan-config-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>VLAN
Config commands
</h3>
<p>
This sub-section explains how to configure the vlan and its member
ports.
</p>
<p>
<strong>config vlan add/del</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is used to add or delete the vlan.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config vlan add/del \<vlan\_\_id\>
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config vlan add 100
This command will create the vlan 100 if not exists.
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<p>
<strong>config vlan member add/del</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command is to add or delete a member port into the already created
vlan.
</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> config vlan member add/del \[-u or --untagged\] \<vlan\_id\>
\<member\_portname\><br> -u will set the port in untagged mode.
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sudo config vlan member add 100 Ethernet0
This command will add Ethernet0 as member of the vlan 100

admin@sonic:~$ sudo config vlan member add 100 Ethernet4
This command will add Ethernet4 as member of the vlan 100.
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
<h2>
<a id="user-content-fdb" class="anchor" href="#fdb" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>FDB
</h2>
<h3>
<a id="user-content-fdb-show-commands" class="anchor" href="#fdb-show-commands" aria-hidden="true"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewbox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path></svg></a>FDB
show commands
</h3>
<p>
<strong>show mac</strong>
</p>
<p>
This command displays the MAC (FDB) entries either in full or partial as
given below.
</p>
<ol>
<li>
show mac - displays the full table
</li>
<li>
show mac -v - displays the MACs learnt on the particular VLAN ID.
</li>
<li>
show mac -p - displays the MACs learnt on the particular port.
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>
Usage:<br> show mac \[-v vlan\_id\] \[-p port\_name\]
</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show mac
No.    Vlan  MacAddress         Port
-----  ------  -----------------  -----------
  1    1000  E2:8C:56:85:4A:CD  Ethernet192
  2    1000  A0:1B:5E:47:C9:76  Ethernet192
  3    1000  AA:54:EF:2C:EE:30  Ethernet192
  4    1000  A4:3F:F2:17:A3:FC  Ethernet192
  5    1000  0C:FC:01:72:29:91  Ethernet192
  6    1000  48:6D:01:7E:C9:FD  Ethernet192
  7    1000  1C:6B:7E:34:5F:A6  Ethernet192
  8    1000  EE:81:D9:7B:93:A9  Ethernet192
  9    1000  CC:F8:8D:BB:85:E2  Ethernet192
 10    1000  0A:52:B3:9C:FB:6C  Ethernet192
 11    1000  C6:E2:72:02:D1:23  Ethernet192
 12    1000  8A:C9:5C:25:E9:28  Ethernet192
 13    1000  5E:CD:34:E4:94:18  Ethernet192
 14    1000  7E:49:1F:B5:91:B5  Ethernet192
 15    1000  AE:DD:67:F3:09:5A  Ethernet192
 16    1000  DC:2F:D1:08:4B:DE  Ethernet192
 17    1000  50:96:23:AD:F1:65  Ethernet192
 18    1000  C6:C9:5E:AE:24:42  Ethernet192
Total number of entries 18
</code></pre>
<ul>
<li>
Optionally, you can specify a VLAN ID or interface name in order to
display only that particular entries
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ show mac -v 1000
No.    Vlan  MacAddress         Port
-----  ------  -----------------  -----------
  1    1000  E2:8C:56:85:4A:CD  Ethernet192
  2    1000  A0:1B:5E:47:C9:76  Ethernet192
  3    1000  AA:54:EF:2C:EE:30  Ethernet192
  4    1000  A4:3F:F2:17:A3:FC  Ethernet192
  5    1000  0C:FC:01:72:29:91  Ethernet192
  6    1000  48:6D:01:7E:C9:FD  Ethernet192
  7    1000  1C:6B:7E:34:5F:A6  Ethernet192
  8    1000  EE:81:D9:7B:93:A9  Ethernet192
  9    1000  CC:F8:8D:BB:85:E2  Ethernet192
 10    1000  0A:52:B3:9C:FB:6C  Ethernet192
 11    1000  C6:E2:72:02:D1:23  Ethernet192
 12    1000  8A:C9:5C:25:E9:28  Ethernet192
 13    1000  5E:CD:34:E4:94:18  Ethernet192
 14    1000  7E:49:1F:B5:91:B5  Ethernet192
 15    1000  AE:DD:67:F3:09:5A  Ethernet192
 16    1000  DC:2F:D1:08:4B:DE  Ethernet192
 17    1000  50:96:23:AD:F1:65  Ethernet192
 18    1000  C6:C9:5E:AE:24:42  Ethernet192
Total number of entries 18

admin@sonic:~$ show mac -p Ethernet192
No.    Vlan  MacAddress         Port
-----  ------  -----------------  -----------
  1    1000  E2:8C:56:85:4A:CD  Ethernet192
  2    1000  A0:1B:5E:47:C9:76  Ethernet192
  3    1000  AA:54:EF:2C:EE:30  Ethernet192
  4    1000  A4:3F:F2:17:A3:FC  Ethernet192
  5    1000  0C:FC:01:72:29:91  Ethernet192
  6    1000  48:6D:01:7E:C9:FD  Ethernet192
  7    1000  1C:6B:7E:34:5F:A6  Ethernet192
  8    1000  EE:81:D9:7B:93:A9  Ethernet192
  9    1000  CC:F8:8D:BB:85:E2  Ethernet192

 13    1000  5E:CD:34:E4:94:18  Ethernet192

 15    1000  AE:DD:67:F3:09:5A  Ethernet192

Total number of entries 18
</code></pre>
</li>
<li>
<p>
<code>sonic-clear fdb \[OPTIONS\]</code>
</p>
<ul>
<li>
Clear FDB table
</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>
Example:
</p>
<pre><code>admin@sonic:~$ sonic-clear fdb all
FDB entries are cleared.
</code></pre>
</li>
</ul>
